Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you wish for one arrow that has fallen or stuck either at front or back, and found the wound healed up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and stays the arrow inside, without disturbing its natural positions,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor finds any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And for another person, who got an arrow wound in their face, and found the wound healed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And he must endure such great pain; and there are no other similar phenomena.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And draw out an arrow at one stroke for the king's princes, where it was stuck in his side.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was slightly leaning towards the right side; and the arrow was entirely out.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called for treatment after it had been stuck for three days. I found the wound extremely narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I sought out all with a subtle test, and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there was pain and hurt throughout her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on a healing plaster for the arm, because the arms did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And appeared to me the head of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the plaster for days and resolved the wound immediately, then the patient suffered long thereafter,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	Until he felt the arrow within his nose; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied an aqua regia medicament to the wound for days until it was opened,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	And I tried it, and felt the tip of the arrow which was penetrating towards its place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted it by opening the wound with this arrow-wounding method, until the head of the arrow became visibly apparent;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and punctured deeply to the inner ends for four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then I stretched it so that the wound opened wide enough for me to insert my tongs, and I did this on both sides, but could not force them through.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Therefore, never stop refining and inventing ways to create tools, until I got possession of one day with very well made tongs,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its shape will be at the end of this chapter, until I try it, and will repair the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	So I would repair it, and then the wound was sealed, and the patient recovered completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	And I told you about the nature of extracting arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you apply your treatment to what I do not say, because books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters will agree on a small amount of good, and on what is current and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find nine works, and the ninth tool, for the removal of things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not emerge from the limbs where they are embedded, rather than in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or at the point where they enter the body, or from another direction;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And if it jumps when entering by itself or at the point of entry, that is the arrow entering the flesh, and it will jump not once but multiple times.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump now, let her go as long as the body is raw inside and well drained of its juices;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And also if it is embedded into the bone, and cannot be removed, if you leave it like this for several days, and remove it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then she jumps out, and if it doesn't jump out, if you pierce through all with a small bore (foret), as long as the bone inside is widened, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if an arrow is embedded in the skull's bone, and goes up to one of the brain's ventricles,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and none of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: if not to cure it straight away, but let it stay until it is equal after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if the arrow reaches just to the joint, this is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow only pierces through the bone and does not reach up to the joint,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and leaves the patient with no bad accidents for some days, if the extraction goes well.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is only deeply embedded and cannot come out, if you administer hot baths internally, as I told you; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if an arrow is placed back into its socket within the body where it cannot be seen, one should search thoroughly for it.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, try to pull it with any suitable tool;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	And if you cannot do so because of the tightness of the wound, or due to the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then widen it as much as making the wound large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and when you can pull out the arrow, if it has ears attached to which it is holding,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if the bone that is stuck in at two places, at the place where you can reach,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as long as you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And make it subtle so that you do not break the arrow, but pull it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it in one go, when the shaft is already deep into your arm, then proceed with its removal, because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding while you're working against it, apply what we have instructed in its treatment within this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and be cautious about the incision near nerves and veins, and do it in such a way that you can remove the arrow without risk.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	whether hot or cold, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the shape they were in when the arrow hit them,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest help for you if you can, and if you cannot, place them according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another side, or if there is any sign of it, or if the skin is swollen in that place where we can see or feel it obviously:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Therefore cut upwards, as long as the forceps can take hold, and then pull: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, rotate your hand around, until it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, let it still, and then start extracting again until it comes out forcefully;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is an arrow in him, once he has it, push the shaft all the way out.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if it's a vein and you see to administer pressure, do so with one of your instruments.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	if the tip of the arrow enters the hair of the tool; and then force it out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is stuck, I force the tool with pointed end entering in order to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is bent, it is necessary that you take all the flesh around or where I am, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it should be done.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if an arrow enters or wounds or is in the belly or bladder or ribs, and it's close by, then you should cover up, if you can cover.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And guard against covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound; this is a task for a skillful person.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat the wound until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used for arrows resembles that of an eagle's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are of many kinds: large, medium-sized, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	by pushing at the tip of the arrow, as this is its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape for pressing and gripping is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins through which one is purified are thirty-one, from which there are sixteen in number.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This means: Two small ones after the ears, which are called 'the two herbs';
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	And the two arteries in the two temples that can be seen;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins that are within two eyelashes, which are called "suckers";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is within the forehead; and the vein that is on the head near the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are at or around the collarbone;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the cheeks above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called 'bubbling';
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which we commonly cure are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, and it is under the left rib, and they call this vein "the arm vein";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "fasting", and it is made up of the cephalic and basilica veins,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call this group of people "the vein from the heart"; and the basilica is either on the right side or under the rib.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And they refer to this as 'the vein of the belly', and it's located above the kidney.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And that is the one which is treated, whose opening becomes apparent through the scrotum.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salve well is the vein that's between the index finger and the ring finger, and it has two parts;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And along the leg and at the foot are three veins: one is located in the bend of the pocket on the left side of the body,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second one is at the ankle on the right side of the body; and the vein that is called "nasce", which is in the ankle on the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are three veins next to these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that are behind the ears helps with colds and headaches, and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of a healthy person, as I have told you, and that your head of the hair behaves well,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the area where the veins are with a coarse cloth; then pinch the neck of the wound with a needle,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until you can see both veins behind the ears in each earlobe over the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Search for this then on your chest, and where you feel the pulse under your chest, if sir it's in need;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the scalpel, and make an incision down to the bone along the vein, then lift your hand all up to the vein upstream,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Cut and remove the skin and the vein well two inches deep, and let out blood until you see it flowing;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then tighten and hold, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already spoken about incision and cautery, or in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding from the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it goes to ancient inflammation,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and also, and habitual conjunctivitis, and within the body of feverish tears are their eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of the surgeon is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And it happens that the patient strains their throat until both veins clearly appear;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And they feel the pulse at both wrists, and then judge from there.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift the hand over the vein at your wrist on top of your index finger, and hold the scalpel nearby,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then lift the vein at the top, and pinch it, just like you did with other veins, and drain the blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton there;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then reapply the bandage and keep it in place until it heals; and we have discussed about this as well as their treatment and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The treatment for the vein in the forehead is as important as the treatment for the cephalic diseases of old, and it includes migraines, and hotness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient twists his neck, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the tool which is called "cautery", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and pierce with your hand or something else, and let out the blood in accordance to the quantity you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the collar for the patient, and bind the vein until it is clean and without any trace of blood;
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	All the same, it is not right for the flames to be too strong; and treat them from across, because the bone is close by, and by chance the flame could break when they are fine.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The treatment for the two veins that are in the two arteries helps the eyes, and at the pulse, and the heat, and in the ear with the ear, and diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their treatment is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting around some ligament, as previously described.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the treatment proceeds, and the treatment should be smooth through, slightly longer than the flame a little wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle and might break by chance; then make it correspond to the blood flow until you have the need for it, and then bind it with cotton, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The treatment of a neck ailment involves cutting through the jugular vein near the nose, and surgery for disorders, and diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	Similarly to migraines and redness that appear in the face, as well as when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the quality of this treatment involves constricting the neck of the patient and then pressing their nose with your left hand;
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	And take the slender flame, and insert it inside the mouth at the space between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well there, and the wound will now begin to drain;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not burn too much below it, and bleed the wound gently according to your need, then rest it for a night, as it recovers very quickly;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is how you treat with heat:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The healing of the two glands helps with squeezing out pus and at the beginning of mixing illnesses, and in the occurrence of diseases, and in congestion, and corrosion, and in herpes, and swelling;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of healing is that the glands are tightened around both ends, just as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be above the neck of the gland, and the gland lie on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then heal the vein so that it is slightly wider along its length, then drain the blood moderately, or as much as necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then redo the operation on the other vein, then release the knot, and gently constrain the veins in the middle.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Let the patient rest until morning, so that the wound heals; and if it does not heal, then one should cut out the diseased tissue.
De la sainie des leivres	Regarding the treatment of wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The treatment of veins in the mouth helps with cleaning the mouth and prevents gum decay, lip cracks, nosebleeds, and internal bleeding.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of health is to make the sick person stand before you, and restrain their neck in the way I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at those two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and know them by what they are black, and because inside them there are thin black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then feel both of them, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If you cut out the largest of each part, and do the same for both upper and lower veins, because it's the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the cure near the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The cure of the veins near the tongue assists after the treatment for head ailments, and this is done at the constriction of the throat, and it deals with eye diseases, and with mouth illnesses;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the surgeon is that when a patient's illness manifests before your hands under the sun, and you raise their tongue, and look at each side revealing a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Therefore, treat both healthily, and do not go too far with them, because they are near the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm that we commonly heal are treated in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or they may be heated with just one flaming firestick, or with a fine olive stick if the sticks are narrow like that of an arm, and it's called 'anesil';
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they should be wide or fine according to the size and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of fire cautery is quite famous and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it requires opening the large veins filled with obvious blood clots, and containing substantial blood and disorder;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive oil cautery:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more refined and pointed, intended for cleaning out subtle veins, or for the presence of subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The treatment of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that affect the throat, and in the neck, and around the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is fitting for the surgeon to treat carefully, and to guard against the artery that is there.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he hits the artery, and bleeding ensues, it is necessary to staunch the bleeding, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And it should not be clamped with fire, but cut like a hare.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open clearly, it is necessary for you to extract it, and change another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want no pain from it, or you pierce through its place with the vein into the arm: it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cover the flame area beforehand, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know the location of the operation, it is necessary that when you remove the arm, you touch the area until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the point of insertion, and then tie the arm, and close the vein before it heals.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And make sure you do not cut into the artery when you see the area inflame, for that is part of the artery: then listen there.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulge up as high as a child's urine, and the veins are red and fine, know that they are veins from the artery: be aware of this.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Then hurry up quickly, place your finger for a long time, then remove your finger when the vein is no longer bleeding, as has often happened.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	The patient must hold their arm, and let it stay like this, without moving the limb. Do so with caution, and don't move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not cleaned, and you need to, and the medicine is not available, if you can, stop the bleeding by pressing on an artery if it's accessible, because the head of the body retreats; clean the wound once done.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of elm bark and cut it, then take one half and bind it well up to the other side;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the wound stops bleeding, that's good; if not, clean it as we have instructed, using powders that stop blood flow.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the dressings are not made wet in many arrangements because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the connection of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The healing of the vein midway assists so that it treats blood from above, and from below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it consists of the basilica and cephalic parts, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And for the surgeon it is necessary to be cautious about the nerve which is below, and if he doesn't go far enough, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it inflates and health is harmed, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any places due to its intricacy, then you must sharpen the surgical instrument beforehand; and feel for the nerve with your hand.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healing of the forehead helps, as it brings blood to the head, and aids in the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is advised to use the olive oil flame or the myrtle flame, for this is the safest of all veins, because there is neither nerve nor artery nearby.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Always, it's necessary to seek the lightest weight, and one should not be upset if it fails the first time, and one should attempt again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance swells some limbs at certain points, even if it fails the first time, but there is no cause for concern.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of cleanliness is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about surgery is that it is practiced solely for maintaining health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and have surgery performed in one of the three veins that are or cut: this means, the cephalic, the femoral, and the basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and surgery should be done at the beginning of prayers while kneeling, and in autumn and after winter following meals, when the signs of fullness are evident;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And whether one should heal on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days and one night.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The treatment of diseases does not have a set time limit, but only when the need is for one day or for food, at all hours and in every situation;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not appropriate to treat children up until 13 years old, nor pregnant women only during the first quarter of their pregnancy up until seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And one should not treat the elderly who have passed sixty years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone seeks to heal himself, no matter how, it is necessary for him to purge his intestines with a gentle laxative.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If he has much of wind retained, so that the veins draw off the excesses causing nuisances to the principal limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor will he be healed who is too full of meats, or drunk, so long as they have strength, or are those with dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if one undertakes to heal after colic pain, vomiting, and stomach discomfort, or frequent urination, pregnancy work, staying awake, sexual intercourse, or anything that weakens the body, as from weapon injury or injuries to oneself.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then refine the fluids, if it's excessive, through meats and drinks and medications, should you have that means;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then in a bath or immersion, if nothing defends it, to refine the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and cleanse you from the vein down to three quarters of the inner part of your back, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and protect yourself from that day of labor, and of pain, and of excess, and from similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And bind and fasten them, and let the bandages be higher than where one is treated, and rub the arm twice or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then gradually adjust the tie, because when it's too tight or too loose, one can't correct the limb without it.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the arm with your hands until the veins swell and are felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then wet the bandages with a little old oil, then place your left hand's finger on that vein below the arm a bit where you want to apply pressure.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	If the vein does not exist and fails to be cut by the sword.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee like strings on a violin, and some of them are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	such that when one places them over the flame, they retreat to the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus one is of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which reason one should have surgeons acquainted with such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if their veins work the first time, it's good; but if not, you may start again a bit near where they were or under quickly, if the area is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the body feels itchy, you should let it rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	In case it comes to an abscess near the skin; don't go into water baths, then try starting the cleansing again if she likes it;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the wound is small or the opening in the skin is subtle and you doubt that not enough blood is coming out as you see, instead pierce it right into the center of the wound straight to the end;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And do it a bit hastily, so that the ears are swollen; for this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see that the ear is inflamed, do not repeat the cure and place a bit of oil on it instead; for it lightens the body from blood, and heals in this area where the oil is applied.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And apply the oil when you perform each cure on veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And when you apply it on the ear, this thyme and honey works well; the oil is too fine if it's in excess, but if it's too large, it disperses and avoids being too heavy.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if it comes about that there is a large abscess, which happens often, just as when the strength of the wound only allows for such an occurrence on that single occasion or when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you are in haste, and place on the wound a sponge moistened with water and wine, let it be warm for just a little while, and then apply it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	it is necessary that you perform this after the bleeding from the vein has subsided, and if it remains on the wound for several days without turning black or green, it does not harm it at all;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see that [the wound], place on it something of myrrh or balsam made into a paste, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times pus and appearance occurred in the health of the basilica: therefore put your hand there, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, then this is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Listen then that you do not apply to any matter what we have said, for it could be done accidentally on the artery; but let him wear one bandage dry to harden the place, then treat with another method of care until he is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And take each according to their strength in their virtue, and the nature of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if the blood is black, let it bleed until it turns red. If you see that it's large, let it continue to flow until it becomes subtle. And if it's too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is suitable for one who is clean and strong, needing extraction of blood, that you make him larger wounds, and let the flames be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is suitable for a physician to be careful and often, and when you need to treat him, cut diagonally rather than straight;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of treatment saves from the spreading of blood and compression of nerves, and it is better than a long cut rather than a wide one.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body requires treatment, it is suitable to give them porridge in juice from green apples; if they are heated, cool them down with blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if the individual has a cold disposition, they should consume before the holy meal a broth with moist ingredients in a syrup mixed with honey or in an aromatic syrup containing spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, along with a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if they faint during the meal, after the release of blood, it is necessary for them to inhale a broth of flesh and a subtle-smelling syrup,
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if they wish to sweat in their arm and again later on, when they are weakened by a great meal, it is necessary that they sweat gradually and according to the amount of its virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if one wishes to pump out their arm after the first cleaning, and they have strong pulses, should they do so seven hours after the first cleaning, or after the new hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wishes to be cleansed another way, then it should be done on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood within the body that has already heated up, and causes fever; so it should be drained in large quantities, and widen the vein until pus emerges.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Then when you have fulfilled all the conditions of cleansing, and place your hand on their pulse when they are healing, so that the disease does not remain in its place.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	And this happens many times, when the surgeons are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not right when you see a dislocated arm and make blood come out the second time, and when the wound has healed, that you press forcefully;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is set straightened, should you quickly extend the arm, for this would be badly done;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it until the second healing; or you apply to the tip of the flame, until the blood that was frozen at the wound flows out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	And place on one part of it a small piece of sulfur set alight, and gently press on it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is bleeding, let it be, do not compress it, until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the need is to drain blood a second time, do so in their own place or another vein, or on the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein under the arm is cleansed from the side of the main vein because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of healing is such that the patient holds their hand in hot water, until the fingers turn red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind them moderately, so that the vein appears well, then heal now through it, not too wide nor too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make them narrow at the ends, and heal well near the wrist joint, and if it cannot come out, then put your hand in hot water, and let the blood flow in the water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is like that, do not put your hand in hot water instead, because you would freeze it more than heat it;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the healing of this vein is safer than all others, for it contains neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The cure for saving the right hand from diseases of the liver is akin to all illnesses, and this is how it is done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Stretch the hand, and soak it in hot water, until the vein becomes visible;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if you heal it from side to side, and if you press on it completely all around, without causing any pain;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not overheat too much at the beginning, because all nerves are entirely stripped of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then immerse your hand in warm water, because if it's frozen in the wound and cannot escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, place on the vein where and seal until it heals quickly, and do this with each case.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The health in the left hand is against the disease of the mouse (or smallpox), and do everything as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The healing of the soul is valued for all diseases that are within the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	just as diseases of the liver, and obstruction of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of old arms and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of this healing is such that patients are healed by being rubbed with hot water, and they are treated on the vein until it heals.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above it goes through much of the kidneys;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Let then the wound heal, or more widely spread outwards, or at the ankle joint, where movement suits.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the leg bone, watch for the nerves that are nearby, and also treat the artery in the same way as cutting; may the flames stop there.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be removed, then place the leg in water, and let it well drain the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it needs healing the first time, then try again the second time above a little bit, because the leg is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about nerves, as we have said, and do the same for the other leg equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The muscles of the sciatic vein are at the knee of strength, and its health is valued for the pain in the hip, when it's due to fresh blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its health is such that the patient sweats or bathes, and tightens above the ankle by扭ing for four inches,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	because otherwise the vein does not open; and if it does open, it benefits in all ways that you can, and even when crossing over;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And value to move it when you have it in your hands, for the head is there, and it is very responsive to human touch.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you cannot find it, if there's no opening or protrusion in front or behind the foot, and towards the small toe, be careful of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And make sure there is such an amount of blood that you see, and then untie the knot, put on cotton and tighten it; she is now cured.
Des sainies de ventouse	Cure with suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Pessaries are made from horns, or spiders, or snakes; and suction therapy is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this suction therapy that involves piercing follows two methods: it can be done with any heat, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And suction therapy performed by piercing and blood extraction is carried out in twelve rounds of the body.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	Of which, one is entirely on top of the head; and the other is under the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two others on two ribs under the collarbone; and the suction cup over the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction cup on the two shoulders; and the suction cup above the pustules;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the suction cups on the two arms; and the suction cups on the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction cups at the ankles; and the suction does not remove blood, but only minor veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And because this does not weaken one, as is done with bleeding of veins;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered, nor with any fire or sense of heat, in any disease that comes from overfullness, until all the bodies are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases one must breathe air or due to habits, then we administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and during and in every period;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are those who, when they need to breathe air, have difficulty with their head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if someone experiences fullness and heat within their face, and on their head, and around the neck, and dimness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who notice a drop of blood in their mouth, have swollen tongues, and are coughing up blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if there are people who think, see through nosebleeds and vomiting, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially during the first month, we instruct to take a breath for three hours after each day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The hygiene of the nose aids in relieving the headache ... that comes from the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of all through the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this suction is part of the hygiene of the cranial area,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it should not be used by those who have a cold constitution, or who are catarrhal, because it causes great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason, those with cold ailments should not use it, nor those whose head has ill diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who often gets healed from it, becomes forgetful, due to this one should place the suction cup slightly further down by the doubt of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Suction at the neck is in the vicinity of the healing of the throat and the basilica; hence it's effective for narrowing towards the anus.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and through the canal of the intestine, and everywhere else, and with replenishment;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it should be done without applying too much pressure, for if she holds too tightly, it could cause dislocation or indigestion or heart problems.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventilation of two ribs under the neck can cause pains in the head, and eye pain and toothache, and in strangulation, and pain at the roots of teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And is in the place of the health of the basilica; and it should be that you instruct the surgeon to move his hand when he places it, not to touch the artery, and not to allow repeated bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation around the chin can cause oral diseases, and gum decay, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and is in the place of the health of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation around the shoulders can cause illness due to heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventilation of the lungs is as valuable as two-thirds of the veins of the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and commands the soldier not to cut too close, for the arm is naked of flesh and it runs over veins and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup on the back is as useful for bleeding from the ground and diseases below it, and it's necessary that the suction cup be large and made of iron, so she can bleed well. And by chance, if it were thin, it would break; I cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs are applied straightforwardly because they draw blood from all over the body and alleviate old pains in the joints, bladder, and kidneys, as well as bloating; and they are located at the knees and ankles, and throughout their use weaken the body over time, leading to debility in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of placing the suction cup is as follows: you place it first while empty and suck continuously, then quickly apply it and move it evenly without stopping. Continue this until you see the skin turning red and inflating, then stop noticing a slight bloodiness; afterwards remove them, and take care with how your body is positioned because there are those who have tough skin and open pores: one should pierce only once in such cases, making broad cuts that are slightly deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the lump is large, it should be pricked twice: the first time to clear the way for the passage of larger blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the hair is very thick, it must be pricked three times; and when we wish to draw out a little blood at a time, we should only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish for some blood, we often repeat the process; and if the hair is thick, we burn until the roots are fully penetrated, and the ends so that the hairs are pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	It is appropriate for those with thick and hard skin, and who have prominent pores, that you grease the spots of the suction cups where the stimulative and dissolving substances are applied:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in a purple oil, or an almond oil, or a seed oil of the cucumber;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it's in the spring, from plants such as garlic, or onion, or chamomile, or any similar type.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take turpentine oil, or balsam oil, or oil from anise, and similar types.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if what one wants to heal is tender flesh and large pores, there should be no oil applied at all,
